### ğŸ”¹ ç·´ç¿’é–±è®€ï¼šå•†æ¥­é›»å­éƒµä»¶

```
To: j.miller@techcorp.com
Cc: a.wilson@techcorp.com
Subject: Upcoming Training Session - April 15

Dear Mr. Miller,

I am writing to inform you about the upcoming staff training session scheduled for April 15, 2025, from 9:00 AM to 4:00 PM at the main conference room.

As discussed in our last meeting, this session will focus on the new customer management software that our company will implement next month. All department managers are required to attend as they will be responsible for training their team members afterward.

Please bring your laptop and the user manual that was distributed last week. If you have not received the manual yet, please contact the IT department as soon as possible.

A detailed agenda will be sent to you three days before the session. If you have any questions or special requirements, please do not hesitate to contact me.

Thank you for your cooperation.

Best regards,
Sarah Johnson
HR Training Coordinator
TechCorp Inc.
Tel: 555-123-4567
s.johnson@techcorp.com
```

#### å•é¡Œï¼š

1. What is the main purpose of this email?  
   (A) To announce a new software implementation  
   (B) To invite managers to a training session  
   (C) To distribute a user manual  
   (D) To share the training agenda  

2. When will the training session take place?  
   (A) Next month  
   (B) Three days from now  
   (C) April 15, 2025  
   (D) Last week  

3. What should Mr. Miller bring to the session?  
   (A) His team members  
   (B) A new software  
   (C) His laptop and user manual  
   (D) The detailed agenda  

4. What will happen if Mr. Miller hasn't received the user manual?  
   (A) He should contact Sarah Johnson  
   (B) He should contact the IT department  
   (C) He should wait for three more days  
   (D) He cannot attend the training  

5. According to the email, what will be sent three days before the session?  
   (A) The user manual  
   (B) A detailed agenda  
   (C) A list of special requirements  
   (D) Contact information  

#### ç­”æ¡ˆï¼š
1. (B)  
2. (C)  
3. (C)  
4. (B)  
5. (B)

```
123 Business Avenue, 15th Floor
Downtown Business District

Important Information:
â€¢ All employees must clear their current workstations by May 28, 2025.
â€¢ Packing materials will be available in the supply room starting May 15.
â€¢ The IT department will handle the transfer of all computer equipment.
â€¢ There will be no business operations on May 30-31 during the move.
â€¢ All employees are expected to report to the new office location on June 1 at regular working hours.
```

#### å•é¡Œï¼š

   (A) To announce a company expansion
   (B) To inform employees about an office move
   (C) To invite employees to an orientation session
   (D) To introduce a new Operations Director

   (B) May 28, 2025
   (C) May 30, 2025

   (D) Robert Thompson

   (B) May 28-31
   (C) May 30-31
   (D) June 1

   (B) An orientation session will be held

```
MARKETING SPECIALIST

TechGlobal Inc., a leading technology company, is seeking a qualified Marketing Specialist to join our growing team.

â€¢ Develop and implement marketing strategies to promote our products and services
```

### ğŸ”¹ ç·´ç¿’é–±è®€ï¼šå…¬å¸å­£åº¦éŠ·å”®å ±å‘Šåœ–è¡¨

è«‹åˆ†æä¸‹é¢çš„éŠ·å”®æ•¸æ“šè¡¨ï¼Œç„¶å¾Œå›ç­”å•é¡Œï¼š

**ABCå…¬å¸ 2024å¹´å­£åº¦éŠ·å”®æ•¸æ“šï¼ˆå–®ä½ï¼šåƒç¾å…ƒï¼‰**

| ç”¢å“é¡åˆ¥ | ç¬¬ä¸€å­£åº¦ | ç¬¬äºŒå­£åº¦ | ç¬¬ä¸‰å­£åº¦ | ç¬¬å››å­£åº¦ | å¹´åº¦ç¸½è¨ˆ |
|----------|----------|----------|----------|----------|----------|
| è¾¦å…¬è¨­å‚™ | 120      | 145      | 132      | 180      | 577      |

#### å•é¡Œï¼š

1. Which product category had the highest total sales for the year?
   (A) Office Equipment
   (B) Electronics
   (C) Furniture
   (D) Stationery

2. In which quarter did ABC Company have the highest total sales?
   (A) First Quarter
   (B) Second Quarter
   (C) Third Quarter
   (D) Fourth Quarter

3. What was the percentage increase in Electronics sales from the first quarter to the fourth quarter?
   (A) About 25%
   (B) About 35%
   (C) About 45%
   (D) About 55%

4. Which product category showed the most consistent sales throughout the year?
   (A) Office Equipment
   (B) Electronics
   (C) Furniture
   (D) Stationery

5. What percentage of the company's total annual sales came from Furniture?
   (A) About 14%
   (B) About 19%
   (C) About 25%
   (D) About 30%

#### ç­”æ¡ˆï¼š
1. (B) - Electronics had the highest total sales of 1,000 thousand dollars.
2. (D) - The Fourth Quarter had the highest total sales of 705 thousand dollars.
3. (B) - (310-230)/230 = 80/230 â‰ˆ 0.35 or about 35% increase.
4. (C) - Furniture showed the least variation between quarters.
5. (B) - 435/2,329 â‰ˆ 0.187 or about 19%.

### ğŸ”¹ ç·´ç¿’é–±è®€ï¼šå“¡å·¥æ»¿æ„åº¦èª¿æŸ¥åœ–è¡¨

è«‹çœ‹ä¸‹é¢çš„å“¡å·¥æ»¿æ„åº¦èª¿æŸ¥åœ–è¡¨ï¼Œç„¶å¾Œå›ç­”å•é¡Œï¼š

**å…¨çƒç§‘æŠ€å…¬å¸å“¡å·¥æ»¿æ„åº¦èª¿æŸ¥çµæœï¼ˆ2024å¹´ï¼‰**

- å·¥ä½œç’°å¢ƒï¼š35%çš„å“¡å·¥çµ¦äºˆ5åˆ†ï¼Œ40%çµ¦äºˆ4åˆ†ï¼Œ15%çµ¦äºˆ3åˆ†ï¼Œ7%çµ¦äºˆ2åˆ†ï¼Œ3%çµ¦äºˆ1åˆ†
- è–ªè³‡å¾…é‡ï¼š20%çš„å“¡å·¥çµ¦äºˆ5åˆ†ï¼Œ35%çµ¦äºˆ4åˆ†ï¼Œ25%çµ¦äºˆ3åˆ†ï¼Œ15%çµ¦äºˆ2åˆ†ï¼Œ5%çµ¦äºˆ1åˆ†
- è·æ¥­ç™¼å±•ï¼š25%çš„å“¡å·¥çµ¦äºˆ5åˆ†ï¼Œ30%çµ¦äºˆ4åˆ†ï¼Œ30%çµ¦äºˆ3åˆ†ï¼Œ10%çµ¦äºˆ2åˆ†ï¼Œ5%çµ¦äºˆ1åˆ†
- å·¥ä½œèˆ‡ç”Ÿæ´»å¹³è¡¡ï¼š30%çš„å“¡å·¥çµ¦äºˆ5åˆ†ï¼Œ25%çµ¦äºˆ4åˆ†ï¼Œ20%çµ¦äºˆ3åˆ†ï¼Œ15%çµ¦äºˆ2åˆ†ï¼Œ10%çµ¦äºˆ1åˆ†
- ç®¡ç†å±¤æ”¯æŒï¼š15%çš„å“¡å·¥çµ¦äºˆ5åˆ†ï¼Œ30%çµ¦äºˆ4åˆ†ï¼Œ35%çµ¦äºˆ3åˆ†ï¼Œ15%çµ¦äºˆ2åˆ†ï¼Œ5%çµ¦äºˆ1åˆ†

#### å•é¡Œï¼š

1. Which aspect of the company received the highest percentage of 5-point ratings?
   (A) Work Environment
   (B) Salary and Benefits
   (C) Career Development
   (D) Work-Life Balance

2. What percentage of employees gave a rating of 3 or lower for Management Support?
   (A) 35%
   (B) 45%
   (C) 55%
   (D) 65%

3. For which aspect did at least 70% of employees give a rating of 4 or 5?
   (A) Work Environment only
   (B) Salary and Benefits only
   (C) Both Work Environment and Career Development
   (D) All aspects except Management Support

4. What is the average rating for Work-Life Balance? (Calculate: (5Ã—30% + 4Ã—25% + 3Ã—20% + 2Ã—15% + 1Ã—10%) Ã· 100%)
   (A) 3.2
   (B) 3.5
   (C) 3.7
   (D) 4.0

5. Which aspect has the highest percentage of dissatisfied employees (ratings of 1 or 2)?
   (A) Work Environment
   (B) Salary and Benefits
   (C) Career Development
   (D) Work-Life Balance

#### ç­”æ¡ˆï¼š
1. (A) - Work Environment received 35% of 5-point ratings, which is the highest.
2. (C) - Management Support: 35% + 15% + 5% = 55% gave a rating of 3 or lower.
3. (A) - Work Environment: 35% + 40% = 75% gave a rating of 4 or 5.
4. (B) - (5Ã—0.3 + 4Ã—0.25 + 3Ã—0.2 + 2Ã—0.15 + 1Ã—0.1) = 3.5
5. (D) - Work-Life Balance: 15% + 10% = 25% gave ratings of 1 or 2.

     - I will send you the files tomorrow. (æˆ‘æ˜å¤©æœƒç™¼æ–‡ä»¶çµ¦ä½ ã€‚)
     - Would you help me with this project? (ä½ é¡˜æ„å¹«æˆ‘è™•ç†é€™å€‹å°ˆæ¡ˆå—ï¼Ÿ)

### ğŸ”¹ æƒ…æ…‹å‹•è©çš„å¦å®šå¼

æƒ…æ…‹å‹•è©çš„å¦å®šå½¢å¼æ˜¯åœ¨æƒ…æ…‹å‹•è©å¾ŒåŠ  "not"ï¼š
- cannot (can't)
- could not (couldn't)
- may not
- might not (mightn't)
- must not (mustn't)
- should not (shouldn't)
- will not (won't)
- would not (wouldn't)

ä¾‹å¥ï¼š
- You cannot use your phone during the meeting. (æœƒè­°æœŸé–“ä½ ä¸èƒ½ä½¿ç”¨æ‰‹æ©Ÿã€‚)
- You shouldn't send confidential information by email. (ä½ ä¸æ‡‰è©²é€šéé›»å­éƒµä»¶ç™¼é€æ©Ÿå¯†ä¿¡æ¯ã€‚)

### ğŸ”¹ æƒ…æ…‹å‹•è©çš„å•å¥

æƒ…æ…‹å‹•è©çš„å•å¥å½¢å¼æ˜¯å°‡æƒ…æ…‹å‹•è©æ”¾åœ¨ä¸»è©å‰ï¼š
- Can you finish this by tomorrow? (ä½ æ˜å¤©èƒ½å®Œæˆé€™å€‹å—ï¼Ÿ)
- Should we reschedule the meeting? (æˆ‘å€‘æ‡‰è©²é‡æ–°å®‰æ’æœƒè­°å—ï¼Ÿ)
- Would you like to join our team? (ä½ æƒ³åŠ å…¥æˆ‘å€‘çš„åœ˜éšŠå—ï¼Ÿ)

---

## âœ… ç·´ç¿’é¡Œï¼šä½¿ç”¨æƒ…æ…‹å‹•è©

1. You (must/can) ________ wear safety equipment in this area. It's required by law.
2. (May/Should) ________ I use your computer for a moment?
3. The new software (can/might) ________ be difficult to learn at first.
4. We (should/will) ________ consider all options before making a decision.
5. You (must/may) ________ be tired after working all day.
6. Employees (can/should) ________ notify their managers if they will be absent.
7. The meeting (will/could) ________ start late because the presenter is stuck in traffic.
8. I (may/have to) ________ work overtime to finish this project on time.
9. (Can/Should) ________ you speak a little louder, please?
10. We (will/might) ________ not be able to deliver the order by Friday.

## ğŸ“š å¤šç›Šé–±è®€æ¸¬é©—ç·´ç¿’ï¼šå‚™å¿˜éŒ„å’Œå ±å‘Šç†è§£

### ğŸ”¹ ç·´ç¿’é–±è®€ï¼šå…¬å¸å…§éƒ¨å‚™å¿˜éŒ„

é–±è®€ä¸‹é¢çš„å‚™å¿˜éŒ„ï¼Œç„¶å¾Œå›ç­”å•é¡Œï¼š

```
MEMORANDUM

TO: All Department Heads
FROM: Jennifer Lee, Human Resources Director
DATE: April 10, 2025
SUBJECT: Annual Performance Review Process

The annual performance review process for all employees will begin on May 1, 2025. Please note the following important dates and actions:

Key Dates:
â€¢ May 1-15: Employees complete self-evaluation forms
â€¢ May 16-31: Managers conduct performance reviews
â€¢ June 1-15: Department heads review and approve evaluations
â€¢ June 20: All reviews must be submitted to HR

Actions Required:
1. Attend the performance review training session on April 20 at 10:00 AM in Conference Room A.
2. Distribute self-evaluation forms to your team members by April 25.
3. Schedule review meetings with each team member during the designated period.
4. Submit all completed review forms to HR no later than June 20.

This year, we will be using the new online evaluation system. Training materials are available on the company intranet under "HR Resources." If you encounter any difficulties with the system, please contact the IT Help Desk at ext. 4444.

Remember that these reviews are essential for determining promotions, salary adjustments, and professional development opportunities for the upcoming fiscal year.

Thank you for your cooperation.
```

#### å•é¡Œï¼š

1. What is the main purpose of this memo?
   (A) To announce a new online evaluation system
   (B) To outline the annual performance review process
   (C) To introduce a new Human Resources Director
   (D) To inform about salary adjustments

2. When must employees complete their self-evaluation forms?
   (A) By April 25
   (B) Between May 1 and May 15
   (C) Between May 16 and May 31
   (D) By June 20

3. What must department heads do by April 25?
   (A) Attend a training session
   (B) Complete self-evaluation forms
   (C) Distribute forms to team members
   (D) Submit reviews to HR

4. Where can employees find training materials for the new system?
   (A) In Conference Room A
   (B) From the IT Help Desk
   (C) From their department heads
   (D) On the company intranet

5. According to the memo, what is one purpose of the performance reviews?
   (A) To evaluate the HR department
   (B) To test the new online system
   (C) To determine promotions
   (D) To schedule training sessions

#### ç­”æ¡ˆï¼š
1. (B)
2. (B)
3. (C)
4. (D)
5. (C)

### ğŸ”¹ ç·´ç¿’é–±è®€ï¼šå¸‚å ´ç ”ç©¶å ±å‘Š

é–±è®€ä¸‹é¢çš„å ±å‘Šæ‘˜éŒ„ï¼Œç„¶å¾Œå›ç­”å•é¡Œï¼š

```
MARKET RESEARCH REPORT: CONSUMER ELECTRONICS INDUSTRY
Prepared by: Global Research Partners
Date: March 15, 2025
For: XYZ Electronics Corporation

EXECUTIVE SUMMARY

This report analyzes current trends in the consumer electronics market with a focus on smartphones, tablets, and wearable devices. Our research indicates that the global market for these products will grow by approximately 8.5% over the next fiscal year, with particularly strong growth in emerging markets (12.3%).

KEY FINDINGS

1. Market Share
   XYZ Electronics currently holds 14% of the global smartphone market, placing it fourth among major manufacturers. This represents a 2% increase from last year but remains 5% behind the market leader.

2. Consumer Preferences
   Survey data shows that consumers increasingly prioritize battery life (76%) and camera quality (68%) over processor speed (45%) when purchasing new smartphones. For tablets, screen size and resolution remain the primary considerations (82%).

3. Emerging Trends
   Wearable technology continues to show strong growth potential, with an estimated market expansion of 15% annually for the next three years. Smart watches represent the largest segment (62%), followed by fitness trackers (28%).

4. Competitive Analysis
   Major competitors have increased their research and development spending by an average of 12% in the past year, with a focus on artificial intelligence features and improved battery technology.

RECOMMENDATIONS

Based on our analysis, we recommend that XYZ Electronics:

1. Increase investment in battery technology and camera systems for the next generation of smartphones.
2. Expand the wearable device product line, particularly in the smart watch category.
3. Strengthen marketing presence in Southeast Asian markets, where brand recognition lags behind competitors by 15-20%.
4. Consider strategic partnerships with software developers to enhance AI capabilities.

Implementation of these recommendations could potentially increase market share by 2-3% within 18 months and position XYZ Electronics more competitively in the wearable technology segment.
```

#### å•é¡Œï¼š

1. What is XYZ Electronics' current position in the global smartphone market?
   (A) First
   (B) Second
   (C) Third
   (D) Fourth

2. According to the report, what percentage of consumers prioritize camera quality when purchasing smartphones?
   (A) 45%
   (B) 62%
   (C) 68%
   (D) 76%

3. Which market is expected to grow the most in the next fiscal year?
   (A) Global smartphone market
   (B) Emerging markets
   (C) Wearable technology market
   (D) Tablet market

4. What is NOT mentioned as a recommendation for XYZ Electronics?
   (A) Investing in battery technology
   (B) Expanding the tablet product line
   (C) Increasing marketing in Southeast Asia
   (D) Forming strategic partnerships

5. By how much has XYZ Electronics' market share increased compared to last year?
   (A) 2%
   (B) 5%
   (C) 8.5%
   (D) 12.3%

#### ç­”æ¡ˆï¼š
1. (D)
2. (C)
3. (C) - 15% annual growth for wearable technology vs. 8.5% for global market and 12.3% for emerging markets
4. (B)
5. (A)

## ğŸ“– åŸºç¤èªæ³•ï¼šå—è©å­å¥ï¼ˆthat-clauseï¼‰

### ğŸ”¹ ä»€éº¼æ˜¯å—è©å­å¥ï¼Ÿ
å—è©å­å¥æ˜¯ç”¨ä¾†ç•¶ã€Œå‹•è©çš„å—è©ã€çš„å­å¥ï¼Œå¸¸ç”± that å¼•å°ï¼ˆä½†å£èªä¸­ often çœç•¥ï¼‰ã€‚

### ğŸ”¹ å¸¸è¦‹å‹•è© + that å­å¥
- say / think / know / believe / hope / expect / hear / notice / understand / tell

### ğŸ”¹ åŸºæœ¬å¥å‹ï¼š
- I think **that** she is right.
- They said **that** the meeting was canceled.
- We believe **that** this product will sell well.

### ğŸ”¹ å¯çœç•¥ that çš„æƒ…æ³
- I know (that) he is busy.
- She said (that) she will call back later.

## âœ… ç·´ç¿’é¡Œï¼šå¡«å…¥æ­£ç¢ºçš„é€£æ¥è©æˆ–å—è©å­å¥å…§å®¹

1. I believe he can do it.  
   â†’ I believe **that** he can do it.

2. She said she would be late.  
   â†’ She said **that** she would be late.

3. We know the office is closed today.  
   â†’ We know **that** the office is closed today.

4. He told me he got the job.  
   â†’ He told me **that** he got the job.

5. They think the plan needs more work.  
   â†’ They think **that** the plan needs more work.

## ğŸ“– åŸºç¤èªæ³•ï¼šå‡è¨­èªæ°£ï¼ˆIf æ¢ä»¶å¥ï¼‰

### ğŸ”¹ ç¬¬ä¸€é¡æ¢ä»¶å¥ï¼ˆç¾å¯¦å¯èƒ½ç™¼ç”Ÿï¼‰
- çµæ§‹ï¼š**If + ç¾åœ¨ç°¡å–®å¼, will + åŸå½¢å‹•è©**
- ç”¨æ³•ï¼šè¡¨ç¤ºã€Œæœªä¾†å¯èƒ½ç™¼ç”Ÿçš„äº‹æƒ…ã€
- ä¾‹å¥ï¼š
  - If it rains, we will cancel the meeting.
  - If you study hard, you will pass the test.

### ğŸ”¹ ç¬¬äºŒé¡æ¢ä»¶å¥ï¼ˆå‡è¨­ä¸å¤ªå¯èƒ½ç™¼ç”Ÿï¼‰
- çµæ§‹ï¼š**If + éå»å¼, would + åŸå½¢å‹•è©**
- ç”¨æ³•ï¼šè¡¨ç¤ºã€Œèˆ‡ç¾åœ¨äº‹å¯¦ç›¸åçš„å‡è¨­ã€
- ä¾‹å¥ï¼š
  - If I were the manager, I would raise your salary.
  - If he had more time, he would join the event.

### ğŸ”¹ é‡è¦èªªæ˜
- be å‹•è©åœ¨ç¬¬äºŒé¡å‡è¨­å¥ä¸­ä¸€å¾‹ç”¨ **were**ï¼ˆä¸è«–ä¸»è©ï¼‰
  - If I **were** you, I wouldnâ€™t do that.

To: All Staff  
From: Nancy Wu, Director of Operations  
Subject: Staff Wellness Program Launch  
Date: May 10, 2025

We are pleased to announce the launch of our new Staff Wellness Program beginning on June 1. This program includes weekly fitness classes, mental health workshops, and access to healthy meals in the cafeteria. Participation is voluntary but highly encouraged.

The goal of this program is to improve work-life balance and overall employee satisfaction. Additional information, including the full schedule and registration details, will be shared via email next week.

If you have any questions, feel free to contact the HR Department.

## ğŸ“– åŸºç¤èªæ³•ï¼šä¸»å‹•èªæ…‹èˆ‡è¢«å‹•èªæ…‹ï¼ˆActive vs. Passive Voiceï¼‰

### ğŸ”¹ ä¸»å‹•èªæ…‹ï¼ˆActive Voiceï¼‰
- ä¸»è©æ˜¯å‹•ä½œçš„åŸ·è¡Œè€…ã€‚
- çµæ§‹ï¼š**ä¸»è© + å‹•è© + å—è©**
- ä¾‹å¥ï¼š
  - The manager **approved** the budget.
  - She **wrote** the report.

### ğŸ”¹ è¢«å‹•èªæ…‹ï¼ˆPassive Voiceï¼‰
- ä¸»è©æ˜¯å‹•ä½œçš„æ¥å—è€…ã€‚
- çµæ§‹ï¼š**ä¸»è© + beå‹•è© + éå»åˆ†è© + (by + è¡Œå‹•è€…)**
- ä¾‹å¥ï¼š
  - The budget **was approved** by the manager.
  - The report **was written** by her.

### ğŸ”¹ å¸¸è¦‹æ™‚æ…‹çš„è¢«å‹•èªæ…‹ï¼š

| æ™‚æ…‹        | è¢«å‹•èªæ…‹çµæ§‹                        | ä¾‹å¥                                      |
|-------------|-------------------------------------|-------------------------------------------|
| ç¾åœ¨ç°¡å–®å¼  | is/am/are + Vpp                     | The task **is done** every day.           |
| éå»ç°¡å–®å¼  | was/were + Vpp                      | The email **was sent** yesterday.         |
| ç¾åœ¨å®Œæˆå¼  | has/have been + Vpp                 | The report **has been submitted**.        |
| æœªä¾†ç°¡å–®å¼  | will be + Vpp                       | The system **will be updated** soon.      |

### ğŸ”¹ è¢«å‹•èªæ…‹å¸¸è¦‹å‹•è©ï¼šsend, give, make, write, approve, assign, build, complete, design, deliver

## âœ… ç·´ç¿’é¡Œï¼šæ”¹å¯«ç‚ºè¢«å‹•èªæ…‹

1. The team submitted the report.  
   â†’ The report **was submitted** by the team.

2. The company will launch a new product.  
   â†’ A new product **will be launched** by the company.

3. They are designing a new logo.  
   â†’ A new logo **is being designed** by them.

4. The HR department has approved the policy.  
   â†’ The policy **has been approved** by the HR department.

5. The technician repaired the computer.  
   â†’ The computer **was repaired** by the technician.

## ğŸ“– åŸºç¤èªæ³•ï¼šæ¯”è¼ƒç´šèˆ‡æœ€é«˜ç´šï¼ˆComparative & Superlativeï¼‰

### ğŸ”¹ æ¯”è¼ƒç´šï¼ˆComparativeï¼‰
- è¡¨ç¤ºã€Œæ¯”â‹¯æ›´â‹¯ã€ï¼Œå¸¸ç”¨çµæ§‹ï¼š**A is + æ¯”è¼ƒç´š + than B**
- è¦å‰‡è®ŠåŒ–ï¼š
  - å–®éŸ³ç¯€å½¢å®¹è©åŠ  -erï¼š**fast â†’ faster**
  - é‡éŸ³åœ¨æœ€å¾Œçš„é›™éŸ³ç¯€åŠ  -erï¼š**narrow â†’ narrower**
  - å¤šéŸ³ç¯€æˆ–ä¸è¦å‰‡ï¼š**more + adj.ï¼ˆimportant â†’ more importantï¼‰**

### ğŸ”¹ æœ€é«˜ç´šï¼ˆSuperlativeï¼‰
- è¡¨ç¤ºã€Œæœ€â‹¯ã€ï¼Œå¸¸ç”¨çµæ§‹ï¼š**A is the + æœ€é«˜ç´š**
- è¦å‰‡è®ŠåŒ–ï¼š
  - **fast â†’ the fastest**
  - **important â†’ the most important**
  - ä¸è¦å‰‡è®ŠåŒ–ï¼š**good â†’ the best**, **bad â†’ the worst**

### ğŸ”¹ å¸¸è¦‹ç”¨æ³•ï¼š
- He is taller than me.
- This is the most useful tool in the office.

## ğŸ“– åŸºç¤èªæ³•ï¼šé—œä¿‚ä»£åè©ï¼ˆRelative Pronounsï¼‰

### ğŸ”¹ ç”¨é€”
é—œä¿‚ä»£åè©ç”¨ä¾†é€£æ¥ä¸»å¥èˆ‡å­å¥ï¼Œç”¨ä¾†èªªæ˜æˆ–è£œå……ä¸»è©æˆ–å—è©ï¼Œå¸¸è¦‹æœ‰ï¼š

| é—œä¿‚ä»£åè© | ç”¨æ³•         | æŒ‡ä»£å°è±¡       | ç¯„ä¾‹                                   |
|------------|--------------|----------------|----------------------------------------|
| who        | ç•¶ä¸»è©       | äºº              | The manager **who** called you is here.|
| whom       | ç•¶å—è©       | äºº              | The employee **whom** we hired is smart.|
| whose      | æ‰€æœ‰æ ¼       | äººæˆ–äº‹ç‰©        | The man **whose** car was stolen is angry.|

| that       | ä¸»è©/å—è©    | äººæˆ–ç‰©ï¼ˆè¼ƒå£èªï¼‰| The laptop **that** she uses is new.   |

### ğŸ”¹ æ³¨æ„
- **that** å¯å–ä»£ who / whichï¼ˆè¼ƒå£èªï¼‰
- é—œä¿‚ä»£åè©å¯çœç•¥ï¼ˆç•¶å…¶ç‚ºå—è©æ™‚ï¼‰ï¼š

## âœ… ç·´ç¿’é¡Œï¼šå¡«å…¥é©ç•¶çš„é—œä¿‚ä»£åè©ï¼ˆwho, whom, whose, which, thatï¼‰

1. The woman ________ answered the phone was very polite.  
   â†’ The woman **who** answered the phone was very polite.  
   *(ä¸»æ ¼ï¼ŒæŒ‡äºº)*

2. This is the report ________ you requested.  
   â†’ This is the report **that** you requested.  
   *(å—æ ¼ï¼ŒæŒ‡äº‹ç‰©ï¼Œä¹Ÿå¯ç”¨ which)*

3. The employee ________ we hired last week is very efficient.  
   â†’ The employee **whom** we hired last week is very efficient.  
   *(å—æ ¼ï¼Œæ­£å¼ç”¨ whomï¼Œå£èªä¸­ä¹Ÿå¯ç”¨ who æˆ–çœç•¥)*

4. Heâ€™s the manager ________ office is on the 5th floor.  
   â†’ Heâ€™s the manager **whose** office is on the 5th floor.  
   *(æ‰€æœ‰æ ¼ï¼ŒæŒ‡äººçš„äº‹ç‰©)*

5. The system ________ crashed yesterday has been restored.  
   â†’ The system **that** crashed yesterday has been restored.  
   *(ä¸»æ ¼ï¼ŒæŒ‡äº‹ç‰©ï¼Œä¹Ÿå¯ç”¨ which)*

## ğŸ“š å¤šç›Šé–±è®€ç·´ç¿’ï¼šå…¬å¸å…§éƒ¨ä¿¡ä»¶

```
Subject: Office Supplies Policy Update

Dear All,

Please be informed that starting next month, we will implement a new policy regarding the ordering of office supplies.

All orders must now go through the purchasing department, and employees will no longer be allowed to purchase supplies directly. This change is part of a cost-saving initiative and will help streamline our procurement process.

Each department must assign one person to handle supply requests and submit a consolidated order at the end of each month.

If you have any questions, please contact Ms. Lydia Wu in the purchasing department.

Thank you for your cooperation.

Sincerely,  
Kevin Huang  
Operations Manager
```

## ğŸ“– åŸºç¤èªæ³•ï¼šä¸å®šè©èˆ‡å‹•åè©ï¼ˆTo-infinitives & Gerundsï¼‰

### ğŸ”¹ ä¸å®šè©ï¼ˆto + Vï¼‰
ç”¨æ–¼è¡¨ç¤º**ç›®çš„ã€è¨ˆåŠƒã€å¸Œæœ›ã€æ±ºå®šç­‰å‹•ä½œ**ï¼š

| ç”¨æ³• | ä¾‹å¥ |
|------|------|
| ç›®çš„ | I study hard **to pass** the exam. |
| è¨ˆåŠƒ | We decided **to hold** the meeting next week. |
| å¸Œæœ› | She hopes **to travel** abroad. |

---

### ğŸ”¹ å‹•åè©ï¼ˆV-ingï¼‰
å¸¸ç•¶ä½œ**ä¸»è©ã€å—è©æˆ–ä»‹ç³»è©å¾Œçš„è£œèª**ä½¿ç”¨ï¼š

| ç”¨æ³• | ä¾‹å¥ |
|------|------|
| ä¸»è© | **Traveling** is fun. |
| å—è© | I enjoy **reading** business books. |
| ä»‹è©å¾Œ | She is good at **solving** problems. |

### ğŸ”¹ éœ€è¦ç‰¹å®šçµæ§‹çš„å‹•è©

| + to Vï¼ˆä¸å®šè©ï¼‰ | + V-ingï¼ˆå‹•åè©ï¼‰ |
|------------------|-------------------|
| want             | enjoy             |
| decide           | finish            |
| plan             | avoid             |
| agree            | consider          |
| hope             | suggest           |
| need             | keep              |

| å‹•è©     | ä¸åŒç”¨æ³•èˆ‡æ„æ€ |

## âœ… ç·´ç¿’é¡Œï¼šé¸æ“‡æ­£ç¢ºçš„ç‰‡èªå‹•è©å¡«ç©º

1. We need to ______ the cause of the error. (call off / find out)
   â†’ We need to **find out** the cause of the error.  
   âœï¸ find out = æŸ¥æ˜ã€ç™¼ç¾ã€‚

   â†’ They decided to **call off** the meeting.  
   âœï¸ call off = å–æ¶ˆã€‚

   â†’ The researcher will **carry out** the experiment tomorrow.  
   âœï¸ carry out = åŸ·è¡Œã€‚

   â†’ We are trying to **look into** what went wrong.  
   âœï¸ look into = èª¿æŸ¥ã€‚

   â†’ He couldn't **figure out** how to solve the issue.  
   âœï¸ figure out = æƒ³å‡ºã€‚

```
Finance Department
```

## ğŸ“– åŸºç¤èªæ³•ï¼šæ¯”è¼ƒç­‰ç´š (Comparatives & Superlatives)

### ğŸ”¹ ç”¨æ³•ç¸½ç´„

| çµæ§‹         | èªªæ˜               | ä¾‹å¥ |
|--------------|--------------------|------|
| æ¯”è¼ƒç´š + than | ç”¨ä¾†æ¯”è¼ƒå…©è€…       | This product is cheaper than that one. |
| the + æœ€é«˜ç´š | è¡¨ç¤ºä¸‰è€…ä»¥ä¸Šæœ€é«˜ç¨‹åº¦ | He is the most experienced engineer. |

### ğŸ”¹ è¦å‰‡è®ŠåŒ–

- å–®éŸ³ç¯€å­—è©åŠ  er/estï¼šfast â†’ faster â†’ fastest  
- ä»¥ y çµå°¾è®Š ier/iestï¼šhappy â†’ happier â†’ happiest  
- å¤šéŸ³ç¯€åŠ  more/mostï¼šefficient â†’ more efficient â†’ most efficient

## ğŸ“– åŸºç¤èªæ³•ï¼šä½¿å½¹å‹•è©ï¼ˆCausative Verbsï¼‰

### ğŸ”¹ èªªæ˜
ä½¿å½¹å‹•è©è¡¨ç¤ºã€Œè®“æŸäººåšæŸäº‹ã€ï¼Œå¸¸è¦‹ç”¨æ³•æœ‰ï¼š**make / let / have / get / help**

### ğŸ”¹ çµæ§‹æ¯”è¼ƒ

| å‹•è©   | çµæ§‹                          | ä¾‹å¥ |
|--------|-------------------------------|------|
| make   | make + å—è© + åŸå½¢å‹•è©        | The boss made her redo the task. |
| let    | let + å—è© + åŸå½¢å‹•è©         | Let me explain it again. |
| have   | have + å—è© + åŸå½¢å‹•è©        | I had the assistant book the tickets. |
| get    | get + å—è© + to + åŸå½¢å‹•è©    | We got him to join the meeting. |
| help   | help + å—è© + (to) åŸå½¢å‹•è©   | She helped me (to) carry the box. |

## ğŸ“– æ–‡æ³•å­¸ç¿’ï¼šåè©å­å¥ï¼ˆNoun Clausesï¼‰

### ğŸ”¹ èªªæ˜

åè©å­å¥å¯æ“”ä»»ä¸»è©ã€å—è©æˆ–è£œèªã€‚å¸¸ç”±ä»¥ä¸‹é€£æ¥è©å¼•å°ï¼š**that, if, whether, what, when, where, why, who, how**ã€‚

### ğŸ”¹ ç”¨æ³•ç¯„ä¾‹

- **ä¸»è©**ï¼š*What she said* was surprising.  
- **å—è©**ï¼šI donâ€™t know *where he went*.

### ğŸ”¹ æ³¨æ„äº‹é …

- åè©å­å¥ä¸­ä¸å€’è£ï¼š
  - âœ… I know *what he wants*.  
  - âŒ I know *what does he want*.

## ğŸ“– æ–‡æ³•å­¸ç¿’ï¼šå½¢å®¹è©å­å¥ï¼ˆAdjective Clausesï¼‰

### ğŸ”¹ èªªæ˜

å½¢å®¹è©å­å¥ä¿®é£¾åè©ï¼Œå¸¸ç”±é—œä¿‚ä»£åè©å¼•å°ï¼ˆwho, whom, whose, which, thatï¼‰ã€‚

### ğŸ”¹ ç”¨æ³•ç¯„ä¾‹

- This is the book **that I mentioned**.  
- The man **whose car was stolen** is reporting it.

### ğŸ”¹ æ³¨æ„äº‹é …

- é—œä¿‚ä»£åè©å¯çœç•¥ï¼ˆè‹¥åœ¨å­å¥ä¸­ç‚ºå—è©ï¼‰ï¼š  
  - âœ… The report (that) you sent is useful.

## ğŸ“– æ–‡æ³•å­¸ç¿’ï¼šå‰¯è©å­å¥ï¼ˆAdverb Clausesï¼‰

### ğŸ”¹ èªªæ˜

å‰¯è©å­å¥ä¿®é£¾å‹•è©ã€å½¢å®¹è©æˆ–æ•´å¥ï¼Œèªªæ˜æ™‚é–“ã€åŸå› ã€æ¢ä»¶ã€è®“æ­¥ç­‰ã€‚å¸¸è¦‹é€£æ¥è©åŒ…æ‹¬ï¼š**because, although, if, when, while, since, as soon as**ã€‚

### ğŸ”¹ ç”¨æ³•ç¯„ä¾‹

- **æ™‚é–“**ï¼šCall me *when you arrive*.  
- **åŸå› **ï¼šWe canceled the trip *because it rained*.  
- **æ¢ä»¶**ï¼šYou can go *if you finish your work*.  
- **è®“æ­¥**ï¼š*Although he was tired*, he kept working.

## ğŸ“– æ–‡æ³•å­¸ç¿’ï¼šä½¿å½¹å‹•è©ï¼ˆCausative Verbsï¼‰

ä½¿å½¹å‹•è©è¡¨ç¤ºã€Œè®“æŸäººåšæŸäº‹ã€ï¼Œå¸¸è¦‹å‹•è©æœ‰ï¼š**make, have, let, get**ã€‚

- **get** + å—è© + to Vï¼šShe got the intern to submit the file.

### ğŸ”¹ æ³¨æ„äº‹é …

- è¢«å‹•èªæ…‹ä¸­ï¼Œmake è¦åŠ  to Vï¼šHe was made **to wait** outside.

## ğŸ“– æ–‡æ³•å­¸ç¿’ï¼šå‹•åè©èˆ‡ä¸å®šè©çš„ä½¿ç”¨å·®ç•°ï¼ˆGerunds vs. Infinitivesï¼‰

### ğŸ”¹ èªªæ˜

æœ‰äº›å‹•è©å¾Œé¢æ¥å‹•åè©ï¼ˆV-ingï¼‰ï¼Œæœ‰äº›æ¥ä¸å®šè©ï¼ˆto + Vï¼‰ï¼Œæœ‰äº›å…©è€…çš†å¯ï¼Œä½†æ„æ€ä¸åŒã€‚

### ğŸ”¹ å¸¸è¦‹ç”¨æ³•

- **å‹•åè©**å¾Œå¸¸è¦‹å‹•è©ï¼šenjoy, consider, avoid, suggest, finish  
- **ä¸å®šè©**å¾Œå¸¸è¦‹å‹•è©ï¼šdecide, hope, plan, want, expect  
- **èªæ„ä¸åŒ**ï¼šstop doingï¼ˆåœæ­¢æ­£åœ¨åšçš„äº‹ï¼‰ vs. stop to doï¼ˆåœä¸‹ä¾†å»åšåˆ¥äº‹ï¼‰

### ğŸ”¹ ç¯„ä¾‹å¥

- I enjoy **reading** business articles.  
- They decided **to launch** a new product line.  
- She stopped **working** to take a call.

## ğŸ“– æ–‡æ³•å­¸ç¿’ï¼šé—œä¿‚å­å¥ï¼ˆRelative Clausesï¼‰

### ğŸ”¹ èªªæ˜

é—œä¿‚å­å¥å¯ç”¨ä¾†ä¿®é£¾åè©ï¼Œä½¿å¥å­æ›´å®Œæ•´ï¼Œå¸¸ä½¿ç”¨çš„é—œä¿‚ä»£åè©æœ‰ï¼š

### ğŸ”¹ å¥å‹èªªæ˜

- The employee **who joined last month** was promoted.  
- The system **that crashed yesterday** has been repaired.  
- They invested in software **which improves efficiency**.

- **éé™å®šå­å¥**ï¼šæä¾›è£œå……è³‡è¨Šï¼ŒåŠ é€—è™Ÿï¼Œå¦‚ï¼š  
  - The CEO, **who is retiring next year**, gave a farewell speech.

## ğŸ“– æ–‡æ³•å­¸ç¿’ï¼šè¢«å‹•èªæ…‹é€²éšï¼ˆPassive Voice - Advanced Usesï¼‰

### ğŸ”¹ èªªæ˜

**è¢«å‹•èªæ…‹**é™¤äº†åŸºæœ¬å¥å‹ï¼ˆbe + p.p.ï¼‰å¤–ï¼Œé‚„æœ‰å¤šç¨®é€²éšç”¨æ³•ï¼š
1. è¢«å‹•é€²è¡Œå¼ï¼šbe + being + p.p.
2. è¢«å‹•å®Œæˆå¼ï¼šhave/has/had been + p.p.
3. Modal + be + p.p.ï¼ˆåŠ©å‹•è© + è¢«å‹•ï¼‰

### ğŸ”¹ ç¯„ä¾‹å¥

- The system **is being updated** by the IT team.  
- The contract **has been signed** by both parties.  
- The documents **must be submitted** before Friday.

```
Subject: Important Notice â€“ Policy Changes to Procurement Process

Dear Colleagues,

Starting next month, the procurement policy will be revised to increase efficiency and accountability. All department purchases above $3,000 must now be pre-approved by the Finance Division. This change is part of a broader restructuring effort aimed at reducing operational costs and preventing redundant spending.

Additionally, a centralized procurement portal will be launched to track orders, manage inventory turnover, and maintain transparency. Training on how to use the new system will be conducted next week by a designated liaison from the IT team.

Please be advised that orders placed outside the portal will not be processed. Your cooperation is critical to the success of this transition.

Regards,  
Procurement Office
```

## ğŸ“š å¤šç›Šé–±è®€ç†è§£ç·´ç¿’

è«‹é–±è®€ä»¥ä¸‹æ®µè½ä¸¦å›ç­”å•é¡Œï¼š

```
To: All Department Heads  
From: CFO Office  
Subject: Preliminary Budget Review for Q3

Dear Managers,

As part of our fiscal planning for the upcoming quarter, all departments are required to submit their preliminary budget reports by June 5th. This initial review will help identify discrepancies, evaluate capital expenditure plans, and anticipate cash flow requirements. Please note that any proposed discretionary spending above $10,000 must be justified in a separate document.

Additionally, all expenses projected as contingent or deferred must be labeled accordingly. Overhead cost estimates should be itemized, and any anticipated liabilities or severance obligations must be flagged for review. 

Your timely cooperation is essential to ensure we maintain solvency and align our expenditures with corporate goals.

Thank you,  
Finance Division
```

````text
From: Operations Department  
Subject: Workflow Optimization Initiative

As part of our company-wide effort to streamline internal processes, we are launching a Workflow Optimization Initiative beginning next Monday. All project managers are required to review their current procedures and identify at least three areas for improvement. Suggestions may include eliminating redundant approval steps, leveraging automation tools, or refining communication channels.

Each team must submit a brief proposal outlining their findings by the end of the week. Selected proposals will be piloted during Q3, with company-wide implementation planned for Q4.

Thank you for your cooperation.

â€“ Operations Department
````

## ğŸ“˜ æ–‡æ³•å­¸ç¿’ï¼šè¤‡é›œå¥ä¸­çš„åè©å­å¥ï¼ˆNoun Clauses in Embedded Structuresï¼‰

### ğŸ”¹ èªªæ˜
åè©å­å¥å¯ç•¶ä¸»è©ã€å—è©ã€è£œèªï¼Œåœ¨è¤‡é›œå¥ä¸­å¸¸è¦‹è¢«å¼•å°èªå¦‚ï¼š
- **that**ã€**whether**ã€**if**
- ç–‘å•è©ï¼ˆwho, what, where, when, why, howï¼‰

### ğŸ”¹ ç¯„ä¾‹å¥
- **What he proposed** was not acceptable.
- She didnâ€™t mention **whether she had submitted the report**.
- It is unclear **how the problem started**.

### ğŸ”¹ å¯¦ç”¨çµæ§‹
- It is + adj. + **that** + S + V ï¼ˆIt is vital that we meet the deadline.ï¼‰
- Whether/If + S + V â€¦ depends on â€¦

---

## âœ… æ–‡æ³•ç·´ç¿’

1. ______ she will join the meeting is still uncertain.  
   (A) Thatâ€ƒ(B) Whetherâ€ƒ(C) Whatâ€ƒ(D) If that  
   **ç­”æ¡ˆï¼šB**

2. It is essential ______ the documents arrive on time.  
   (A) whatâ€ƒ(B) ifâ€ƒ(C) thatâ€ƒ(D) whether  
   **ç­”æ¡ˆï¼šC**

3. No one knows ______ caused the server to crash.  
   (A) whatâ€ƒ(B) thatâ€ƒ(C) how muchâ€ƒ(D) if  
   **ç­”æ¡ˆï¼šA**

4. ______ we should relocate the branch office was debated.  
   (A) Thatâ€ƒ(B) Whatâ€ƒ(C) Whetherâ€ƒ(D) If that  
   **ç­”æ¡ˆï¼šC**

5. I wonder ______ he will accept the counteroffer.  
   (A) howâ€ƒ(B) whyâ€ƒ(C) whetherâ€ƒ(D) which  
   **ç­”æ¡ˆï¼šC**

## ğŸ“š å¤šç›Šé–±è®€ç†è§£ç·´ç¿’

### é–±è®€çŸ­æ–‡

````text
To: All Staff  
From: Operations Manager  
Subject: Change in Procurement Procedure

Starting next Monday, all procurement requests must be submitted through the new digital platform, ProcureNow. This change aims to streamline our purchasing process and ensure better compliance with internal audit policies. All staff members are required to complete a 30-minute training module on the platform before submitting their first request.

The old paper-based form will no longer be accepted after this Friday. For assistance or questions regarding access, please contact your department liaison or the IT support team.

Thank you for your cooperation.
````

## ğŸ“– æ–‡æ³•å­¸ç¿’ï¼šå€’è£å¥å‹ï¼ˆInversion Structuresï¼‰

### ğŸ”¹ èªªæ˜

å€’è£å¥å°‡å‰¯è©æˆ–ä»‹ç³»è©ç‰‡èªæ”¾åœ¨å¥é¦–ï¼Œå°è‡´ä¸»è©èˆ‡å‹•è©èªåºé¡›å€’ã€‚å¸¸ç”¨æ–¼å¼·èª¿ã€æ¢ä»¶ã€çœç•¥ if çš„å‡è¨­èªæ°£ç­‰èªå¢ƒä¸­ã€‚

### ğŸ”¹ å¸¸è¦‹å¥å‹

- **Rarely / Never / Seldom / Hardly / Little / Not only + åŠ©å‹•è© + ä¸»è© + åŸå½¢å‹•è©**
  - e.g., **Rarely have we seen** such dedication.
- **Only if / Only after / Only when / Not until + åŠ©å‹•è©å€’è£**
  - e.g., **Only after the meeting was over did he speak.**
- **Had + ä¸»è© + p.p., ä¸»è© + would/could/might have + p.p.**
  - e.g., **Had I known**, I would have acted sooner.

## ğŸ“– æ–‡æ³•å­¸ç¿’ï¼šåè©å­å¥ï¼ˆNoun Clausesï¼‰

### ğŸ”¹ èªªæ˜

åè©å­å¥åœ¨å¥ä¸­æ“”ä»»ä¸»è©ã€å—è©æˆ–è£œèªã€‚å¸¸è¦‹å¼•å°è©åŒ…æ‹¬ï¼š

- **that**ï¼šI believe **that he is honest**.
- **if / whether**ï¼šI donâ€™t know **if she will attend**.
- **wh- ç–‘å•è©ï¼ˆwhat, who, when, where, why, howï¼‰**ï¼šTell me **what you need**.

åè©å­å¥ä½œç‚ºä¸»è©æ™‚å¸¸ç”¨è™›ä¸»è© it ç½®å‰ï¼š

- **It is important that you arrive early.**
- **Itâ€™s unclear whether the event will continue.**

````text
The companyâ€™s mid-year financial results reflect strong performance across all major departments. ## ğŸ“š å¤šç›Šé–±è®€ç†è§£ç·´ç¿’
````

````text
To: All Division Heads  
From: Executive Office  
Subject: Annual Budget Planning Guidelines

As we prepare for the next fiscal year, please begin submitting your initial budget drafts by the end of this month. These drafts should reflect current expenditure trends, forecasted departmental needs, and potential capital investments.

Each division is expected to justify budget increases with performance data and strategic goals. The executive team will review all submissions during the first week of next month. A follow-up meeting will be scheduled for departments requiring major adjustments.

Thank you for your cooperation and timely submissions.
````

---

````text
Subject: Staff Morale Improvement Measures

In light of recent feedback collected during our quarterly employee survey, HR will implement a series of initiatives to enhance workplace morale and productivity. These include flexible work schedules, an internal mentorship program, and the launch of a peer-recognition platform.

The feasibility of additional measures such as wellness stipends and quarterly team outings is under review. All managers are requested to gather input from their respective teams regarding the proposed changes and submit summaries by the end of next week.

We believe these initiatives will lead to better engagement, reduced turnover, and a more collaborative work environment.
````

````text
Effective immediately, all business travel must be pre-approved through the updated online system. This change aims to streamline the reimbursement process and reduce errors associated with manual entry. Any travel not entered into the system beforehand will not be eligible for reimbursement.

Should you have any questions, please contact the Finance Help Desk.
````

````text
To: Marketing Department  
From: Strategy Team  
Subject: Adjustment to Q4 Advertising Budget

Due to the downturn in consumer spending and increased tariffs on imported goods, the advertising budget for Q4 will be reduced by 15%. All campaign leads are required to reallocate resources accordingly and submit revised plans by next Friday.

The goal is to mitigate unnecessary costs while maintaining brand visibility. Teams are encouraged to explore lower-cost outreach options, such as email marketing and webinars. Performance will be reviewed monthly under stricter scrutiny to ensure ROI benchmarks are met.

For further clarification, please contact your assigned liaison officer.
````

---

### å•é¡Œï¼š

   (A) Poor campaign performance  
   (B) New competitors  
   (C) Economic decline and higher tariffs  
   (D) Changes in team structure  
   **ç­”æ¡ˆï¼šC**

   (B) Submit new strategies  
   (C) Increase social media usage  
   (D) Hire new staff  
   **ç­”æ¡ˆï¼šB**

   (A) Reduce product prices

## ğŸ“– æ–‡æ³•å­¸ç¿’ï¼šæ¯”è¼ƒç´šèˆ‡å€æ•¸è¡¨é”ï¼ˆComparatives & Multipliersï¼‰

### ğŸ”¹ èªªæ˜

æ¯”è¼ƒç´šç”¨ä¾†è¡¨é”å…©è€…ä¹‹é–“çš„å·®ç•°ï¼Œå¸¸è¦‹å¥å‹èˆ‡å‰¯è©åŒ…æ‹¬ï¼š

- **æ¯”è¼ƒç´š + than**  
  e.g., The new model is **faster than** the previous one.

- **by + æ•¸å­— + å€æ•¸ + æ¯”è¼ƒç´š**  
  e.g., Sales increased **by 25%**, making it **three times higher than** last year.

- **å€æ•¸ + as + å½¢å®¹è©/å‰¯è© + as**  
  e.g., This product is **twice as efficient as** its competitor.

- **far / much / significantly / slightly + æ¯”è¼ƒç´š**  
  e.g., The new plan is **much more effective**.

## ğŸ“š å¤šç›Šé–±è®€ç†è§£ç·´ç¿’

````text
To: All Department Supervisors  
From: Human Resources Department  
Subject: Annual Compensation Benchmarking

As part of our annual review process, the HR team will conduct a compensation benchmarking analysis starting next week. The objective is to ensure our salary structures remain competitive within the industry and across regional offices. Data will be collected from both internal payroll systems and external labor market surveys.

Each department will be contacted to provide role-specific job descriptions and current salary bands. This initiative is expected to support future promotion and recruitment strategies.

If your department requires assistance, please contact the designated HR analyst.
````

## ğŸ“– æ–‡æ³•å­¸ç¿’ï¼šçœç•¥ if çš„æ¢ä»¶å¥ï¼ˆInverted Conditionalsï¼‰

### ğŸ”¹ èªªæ˜

åœ¨æ­£å¼æˆ–æ›¸é¢èªä¸­ï¼Œå¸¸å°‡æ¢ä»¶å¥ä¸­çš„ "if" çœç•¥ï¼Œä¸¦å°‡å¥å­æ”¹ç‚ºå€’è£å¥å½¢å¼ï¼Œå¢åŠ èªæ°£çš„æ­£å¼æ€§èˆ‡è®ŠåŒ–ï¼š

### ğŸ”¹ çµæ§‹å…¬å¼

- **Should + ä¸»è© + åŸå½¢å‹•è©ï¼Œä¸»å¥...**
  - â¤ Should you have any questions, please contact us.
- **Had + ä¸»è© + éå»åˆ†è©ï¼Œä¸»å¥...**
  - â¤ Had we known earlier, we would have changed the plan.
- **Were + ä¸»è© + to + åŸå½¢å‹•è©ï¼Œä¸»å¥...**
  - â¤ Were she to resign, the team would struggle.

## ğŸ“– æ–‡æ³•å­¸ç¿’ï¼šæ™‚é–“èˆ‡æ¢ä»¶å­å¥çš„çœç•¥ï¼ˆElliptical Clauses in Time & Conditionï¼‰

### ğŸ”¹ èªªæ˜

ç•¶æ™‚é–“ï¼ˆwhen, after, while ç­‰ï¼‰æˆ–æ¢ä»¶ï¼ˆif, unless ç­‰ï¼‰å­å¥èˆ‡ä¸»å¥ä¸»è©ä¸€è‡´æ™‚ï¼Œå¯çœç•¥é€£æ¥è©èˆ‡ä¸»è©ï¼Œä¿ç•™å‹•è©åˆ†è©çµæ§‹ï¼Œç¨±ç‚º Elliptical Clauseã€‚

### ğŸ”¹ æ™‚é–“å‰¯è©å­å¥çš„çœç•¥ï¼š

- **åŸå¥**ï¼šWhen he enters the room, everyone looks at him.  
- **çœç•¥å¾Œ**ï¼šEntering the room, everyone looks at him.

### ğŸ”¹ æ¢ä»¶å‰¯è©å­å¥çš„çœç•¥ï¼š

- **åŸå¥**ï¼šIf you are given the opportunity, you should take it.  
- **çœç•¥å¾Œ**ï¼šGiven the opportunity, you should take it.

````text
To: All Employees  
From: Legal Compliance Department  
Subject: Temporary Moratorium on New Vendor Contracts

Due to recent regulatory changes, a temporary moratorium on establishing new vendor contracts is now in effect. During this period, no departments may initiate or finalize agreements with external suppliers. All pending contracts must be reviewed by the legal team prior to execution.

This measure aims to ensure compliance with updated financial governance standards. The moratorium is expected to last until the end of the fiscal quarter. Additional guidance will be distributed during next weekâ€™s compliance seminar.
````

## ğŸ“– æ–‡æ³•å­¸ç¿’ï¼šå¼·èª¿å‰¯è©é–‹é ­å¥å‹ï¼ˆEmphatic Adverbs at Sentence Startï¼‰

### ğŸ”¹ èªªæ˜

æŸäº›å‰¯è©ï¼ˆå¦‚ï¼šOnly then, Never, Rarely, Not until, Hardly...whenï¼‰è‹¥æ”¾åœ¨å¥é¦–ä»¥è¡¨å¼·èª¿ï¼Œæœƒè§¸ç™¼**å¥å­å€’è£**ï¼ˆåŠ©å‹•è©æå‰ï¼‰ï¼š

- **Only then** did he understand the message.
- **Never** have we seen such results.
- **Hardly** had I arrived **when** the meeting began.

é€™èˆ‡ä¸€èˆ¬å€’è£å¥ä¸åŒï¼Œç‰¹åˆ¥å‡ºç¾åœ¨å…·æœ‰**å¦å®šã€å‰¯è©ç‰‡èªæˆ–é »ç‡å‰¯è©**é–‹é ­æ™‚ã€‚

### ğŸ”¹ å¸¸è¦‹å¥é¦–å¼·èª¿å‰¯è©

| å‰¯è©ç‰‡èª       | ä¸­æ–‡æ„æ€         |
|----------------|------------------|
| Only then      | ç›´åˆ°é‚£æ™‚         |
| Never          | å¾æœª             |
| Rarely         | å¾ˆå°‘             |
| Not until      | ç›´åˆ°...æ‰        |
| Seldom         | å¾ˆå°‘             |
| Scarcely...when| å‰›...å°±          |
| Hardly...when  | å‰›...å°±          |

## ğŸ“š å¤šç›Šé–±è®€ç†è§£ç·´ç¿’

````text
To: All Regional Managers  
From: VP of Sales Strategy  
Subject: Quota Allocation Policy Update

Beginning next quarter, the Sales Department will implement a revised quota allocation model. Instead of assigning fixed targets, quotas will now be calculated using a weighted formula based on territory size, past performance, and projected growth. This change is designed to create a more equitable and data-driven framework for performance assessment.

Regional managers are advised to review the new methodology in the shared documentation folder and prepare questions for the Q&A session scheduled next Wednesday.

Failure to meet the revised targets for two consecutive quarters may result in performance reviews or territory reassignment.
````

## ğŸ“– æ–‡æ³•å­¸ç¿’ï¼šä¸»è©çœç•¥å¥ï¼ˆElliptical Sentencesï¼‰

### ğŸ”¹ èªªæ˜

ä¸»è©çœç•¥å¥æ˜¯å°‡ **èˆ‡ä¸»è¦å­å¥ç›¸åŒçš„ä¸»è©** åœ¨å‰¯è©å­å¥ä¸­çœç•¥ï¼Œä½¿å¥å­æ›´ç°¡æ½”ã€‚é€šå¸¸å‡ºç¾åœ¨ if, while, though, because ç­‰é–‹é ­çš„å‰¯è©å­å¥ä¸­ã€‚

- **å®Œæ•´å¥**ï¼šIf you are given the opportunity, you should act fast.  
- **çœç•¥å¥**ï¼šIf given the opportunity, you should act fast.

### ğŸ”¹ å¸¸è¦‹çœç•¥é–‹é ­ï¼š

- **If + p.p. / V-ing / adj.**  
- **When / While / Though + p.p. / V-ing / adj.**

---

## âœ… æ–‡æ³•ç·´ç¿’

è«‹é¸å‡ºç¬¦åˆèªæ„çš„ä¸»è©çœç•¥å¥é¸é …ï¼š

1. ______ prepared, the team would have succeeded.  
   (A) Ifâ€ƒ(B) Hadâ€ƒ(C) If beingâ€ƒ(D) If better  
   **ç­”æ¡ˆï¼šC**

2. If ______ early, you might catch the train.  
   (A) leftâ€ƒ(B) leaveâ€ƒ(C) leavingâ€ƒ(D) leaving early  
   **ç­”æ¡ˆï¼šD**

3. Though ______, she accepted the offer.  
   (A) surprisingâ€ƒ(B) surprisedâ€ƒ(C) was surprisedâ€ƒ(D) surprisedly  
   **ç­”æ¡ˆï¼šB**

4. While ______ cautious, the manager remained open to new ideas.  
   (A) beâ€ƒ(B) beingâ€ƒ(C) isâ€ƒ(D) was  
   **ç­”æ¡ˆï¼šB**

5. If ______ properly, the device will last for years.  
   (A) maintainâ€ƒ(B) maintainedâ€ƒ(C) maintainingâ€ƒ(D) maintainable  
   **ç­”æ¡ˆï¼šB**

## ğŸ“š å¤šç›Šé–±è®€ç†è§£ç·´ç¿’

````text
To: Sales Department  
From: Marketing Director  
Subject: Temporary Price Adjustment Policy

Due to seasonal demand and supply chain constraints, we will implement a temporary price adjustment for selected electronic accessories starting next Monday. These changes will affect items under the SmartTech and AeroGear brands.

All sales representatives are required to inform customers of the new pricing. The updated catalog and pricing chart will be available in the internal portal by Friday.

Please note that any price discrepancies during this period must be reported immediately to the regional supervisor. A waiver may be applied on a case-by-case basis pending management review.
````

## ğŸ“– æ–‡æ³•å­¸ç¿’ï¼šçœç•¥å¥ï¼ˆElliptical Constructionsï¼‰

### ğŸ”¹ èªªæ˜

çœç•¥å¥æ˜¯ä¸€ç¨®åˆªé™¤é‡è¤‡éƒ¨åˆ†ä»¥ä½¿å¥å­æ›´ç°¡æ½”çš„æ–‡æ³•çµæ§‹ï¼Œé€šå¸¸ç™¼ç”Ÿåœ¨æ¯”è¼ƒå¥ã€æ¢ä»¶å¥èˆ‡å°ç­‰å¥ä¸­ï¼š

- æ¯”è¼ƒå¥çœç•¥ï¼š  
  - *He earns more than she (does).*
- æ¢ä»¶å¥çœç•¥ï¼š  
  - *(If) necessary, contact the supervisor.*
- å°ç­‰å¥çœç•¥ï¼š  
  - *John can speak French, and Mary (can speak French), too.*

## âœ… æ–‡æ³•ç·´ç¿’

1. I will attend the meeting if necessary. = ______  
   (A) Necessary, I will attend the meeting.  
   (B) Attending if necessary.  
   (C) If is necessary, I will attend.  
   (D) Attending is necessary.  
   **ç­”æ¡ˆï¼šA**

   (B) Mike does  
   (C) Mike is  
   (D) Mike  
   **ç­”æ¡ˆï¼šC**

   (A) by mail  
   (B) submit by mail  
   (C) submission mail  
   (D) to mail  
   **ç­”æ¡ˆï¼šA**

   (A) If she invited, she will attend.  
   (B) She is invited, she will attend.  
   (C) If she is invited, she will attend.  
   (D) Invite her and she will attend.  
   **ç­”æ¡ˆï¼šC**

   (D) does  
   **ç­”æ¡ˆï¼šD**

## ğŸ“š å¤šç›Šé–±è®€ç†è§£ç·´ç¿’

è«‹é–±è®€ä»¥ä¸‹æ®µè½ä¸¦å›ç­”å•é¡Œï¼š

````text
To: All Treasury Department Staff  
From: Chief Risk Officer  
Subject: Policy Update on Liquidity and Leverage Controls

In response to increased market volatility, we are updating our internal policies regarding liquidity thresholds and leverage limits. Effective immediately, all departments must conduct weekly solvency ratio reviews and report any anomalies by Friday noon.

In addition, all new outlays above $100,000 must be pre-approved by the Executive Finance Committee. Failing to comply with this policy will result in a freeze on discretionary budgets for the following quarter.

A training session on updated ledgering protocols and provisioning standards will be held on Thursday. Attendance is mandatory for all financial officers and analysts.
````

---

   (A) Employee feedback  
   (B) Market instability  
   (C) Technology upgrades  
   (D) Merger activities  
   **ç­”æ¡ˆï¼šB**

   (A) Submit tax reports  
   (B) Request funding  
   (C) Review solvency ratios  
   (D) Hold liquidity drills  
   **ç­”æ¡ˆï¼šC**

   (A) Hiring new staff  
   (B) Large financial outlays  
   (C) Department restructuring  
   (D) Budget freeze enforcement  
   **ç­”æ¡ˆï¼šB**

4. What is the consequence of non-compliance?  
   (A) Staff dismissal  
   (B) Audit failure  
   (C) Freezing of discretionary budgets  
   (D) Cancellation of promotions  
   **ç­”æ¡ˆï¼šC**

# ç¬¬äº”åä¸ƒå¤©ï½œBusiness Proposal Follow-up

---

## ğŸ“˜ é–±è®€æ–‡ç« ï¼ˆç´„ 270 å­—ï¼‰

**Subject:** Re: Marketing Proposal â€“ Partnership Opportunity

Dear Ms. Jenkins,

Thank you for your recent proposal regarding a strategic marketing partnership between our two companies. We have reviewed your suggested approach thoroughly and appreciate the time and effort your team invested in outlining the potential benefits.

After internal discussions, we believe there is strong potential in collaborating on the Q4 campaign, particularly in terms of reaching new customer segments in Southeast Asia. However, before we proceed, we would like to request further clarification on your projected budget breakdown and expected ROI.

Additionally, we propose scheduling a virtual meeting sometime next week to align our respective objectives and finalize the action plan. Please let us know your availability on Tuesday or Thursday morning, so we can coordinate accordingly.

We are optimistic about the value this collaboration can bring and look forward to working closely with your team.

Best regards,  
Alan Morris  
Regional Marketing Director  
Optimax Solutions Ltd.

---

# ç¬¬äº”åå…«å¤©ï½œInternal Memo â€“ Policy Update

---

## ğŸ“˜ é–±è®€æ–‡ç« ï¼ˆç´„ 270 å­—ï¼‰

**Subject:** Updated Remote Work Policy â€“ Effective August 1

To: All Employees  
From: HR Department  
Date: July 5  

We are writing to inform you of the updated remote work policy, which will take effect on August 1. After collecting feedback from multiple departments and evaluating productivity data over the past six months, the management team has decided to implement a hybrid work model.

Under this new policy, employees are expected to be in the office at least three days per week. Specific schedules may vary depending on team needs and managerial discretion. Exceptions can be requested through the HR portal, and all accommodations will be reviewed on a case-by-case basis.

Additionally, the company will continue to support remote collaboration by maintaining access to essential tools such as video conferencing software, cloud-based project management systems, and VPN services.

Should you have any questions regarding the updated policy, please reach out to your supervisor or contact HR directly. We appreciate your cooperation and flexibility as we strive to balance efficiency with employee well-being.

---
